الكلي ينقسم كما عرفنا إلى جزئيات وهذه الجزئيات تكون أنواعا كانقسام الجنس إلى أنواعه وتكون أصنافا أو أفرادا كانقسام النوع إلى أصنافه أو أفراده ومثال انقسام النوع إلى أصنافه انقسام الإنسان إلى أبيض وأسود وأحمر وأصفر وانقسامه إلى إفريقي وآسيوي وأوروبي وانقسامه إلى ذكي وبليد وما بينهما وانقسامه إلى صحيح وعليل وانقسامه إلى مؤمن وكافر وإلى تقي وفاجر وهكذا لا تكاد تنحصر تقسيمات الأصناف باختلاف الاعتبارات ومثال انقسام النوع إلى أفراده انقسام الإنسان إلى سعد وباسم وجميل وسعدية وباسمة وجميلة وهكذا إلى سائر أفراد نوع الإنسان والجزئيات المشتركة في معنى يطلق هذا المعنى على كل منها يمكن أن تجمع ذهنا في كلي واحد فحيث نجد أشياء مشتركة في معنى جامع لها ولو بوصف من الأوصاف يمكن أن نجمعها تحت اسم كلي جامع مشتق من هذا الوصف المشترك فوحيد القرن كلي يمكن أن يطلق على كل حيوان ذي قرن واحد فقط وذوات القوائم الأربع كلي نجمع تحته كل حيوان يمشي على أربع قوائم والثديي كلي نجمع تحته كل حيوان يرضع بثدي له أو هو من نوع ما يرضع بثدي له والأبيض كلي نجمع تحته كل ذي لون أبيض من أي نوع ومن أي جنس والطويل كذلك وهكذا إلى ما لا حصر له والكل يتألف كما عرفنا سابقا من أجزاء والأجزاء البسيطة أو المركبة قابلة للتركيب بوجه ما سواء أكان هذا التركيب على وجه له نظير في التركيبات الطبيعية أو على وجه آخر يفترضه الخيال وكل مركب قابل للتحليل إلى أجزائه الصغيرة وعناصره الأولى. أ - عمليات التقسيم والجمع فمن الوسائل النافعة جدا أو الضرورية في كثير من الأحيان في مجال اكتساب المعارف الحسية أو الاستنباطية النظرية أو العملية عمليات التقسيم والجمع أي تقسيم الكلي إلى جزئياته وإلى أصنافه وجمع الجزئيات المتفرقة في كلياتها ففي التقسيم لكليات الأشياء تيسير لدراسة كل قسم دراسة مستوعبة أو أكثر إحاطة بالصفات والخصائص وبعد الدراسة الجزئية التفصيلية واستنباط الأحكام منها تعود العملية إلى جمع الأحكام الجزئية المتماثلة أو جمع الأشباه والنظائر وإعطائها صفة القاعدة الكلية الشاملة لأفراد الصنف أو لأفراد النوع أو لأفراد الجنس القريب أو البعيد ففي هذا الجمع اختصار للمعرفة وإيجاز فيها دون الإخلال بالمقصود منها ودون الإخلال بتطبيقاتها بل هي أيسر وأحكم لضبط الجزئيات دون إخلال وفي هذا الجمع أيضا معرفة جديدة تكتسب فيها كليات الأحكام ومن طبيعة الفكر ميله دائما إلى إدراك كليات الأحكام وكليات القضايا ليوفر على نفسه حفظ كل جزئي وصفاته وخصائصه وليستوعب في أقصر مدة أوسع ما يمكن من معرفة وليتيسر له تطبيق ما استوعب من أحكام كلية على كل جزئي يتعرض له من الجزئيات الداخلة في عموم ما ينطبق عليه الحكم الكلي ولو لم يكن له بخصوصه سابق معرفة به لذلك يلجأ الباحثون بعد عمليات البحث إلى استخلاص الأحكام الكلية العامة وصوغ القواعد الكلية والقوانين العلمية ثم يضعون هذه الأحكام والقواعد والقوانين أسسا يبنى عليها وينتفع بها في كل مجالات المعرفة النظرية والتطبيقية
Research Tools: Operations of Division and Collection, Analysis and Composition. The universal is divided - as we have known - into particulars, and these particulars become types, like the division of genus into its species, and they become varieties or individuals, like the division of species into its varieties or its individuals. An example of the division of species into its varieties: the division of human into white, black, red, yellow; and its division into African, Asian, European; and its division into intelligent, stupid and what is between them; and its division into healthy and sick; and its division into believer and disbeliever, and into pious and immoral; and so on, the divisions of varieties are almost unlimited by different considerations. An example of the division of species into its individuals: the division of human into Sa'd, Basim, and Jamil, and Sa'diyah, Basimah, and Jamilah, and so on to the rest of the individuals of the human species. Particulars that share a meaning that this meaning is applied to each of them can be collected mentally into one universal. So wherever we find things sharing a comprehensive meaning, even by one description, we can collect them under a collective universal name derived from this shared description. Thus unicorn is a universal that can be applied to every animal with only one horn. And quadruped is a universal under which we collect every animal that walks on four legs. And mammal is a universal under which we collect every animal that suckles with its breast, or is of the kind that suckles with its breast. And white is a universal under which we collect everything having white color from any species and any genus. And tall likewise. And so on ad infinitum. The whole - as we have known previously - consists of parts. The simple or composite parts are liable to composition in some way, whether this composition is of a kind that has a counterpart in natural compositions, or of another kind that the imagination posits. And every composite is subject to analysis into its small parts and its primary elements. A - Operations of Division and Collection: Among the very useful or often necessary means in the field of acquiring sensory or inferential knowledge, theoretical or practical, are the operations of division and collection, i.e., dividing the universal into its particulars and its varieties, and collecting scattered particulars into their universals. For in the division of universals of things, there is facilitation for studying each section comprehensively, or more encompassing of attributes and characteristics. And after the detailed partial study and the deduction of judgments from them, the operation returns to collecting similar partial judgments, or collecting similars and analogues, and giving them the character of the universal rule that encompasses the individuals of the variety, or the individuals of the species, or the individuals of the proximate or remote genus. For in this collection there is a summarization of knowledge and conciseness in it without violating its intended purpose, and without violating its applications; rather it is easier and more precise for controlling the particulars without violation. And in this collection there is also new knowledge, in which universals of judgments are acquired. And it is in the nature of the mind to always tend to perceive universals of judgments and universals of propositions, to spare itself the memorization of every particular and its attributes and characteristics, and to encompass in the shortest time the widest possible knowledge, and to facilitate for itself the application of what it has encompassed of universal judgments to every particular it encounters among the particulars that fall under the generality to which the universal judgment applies, even if it had no prior knowledge of it specifically. Therefore, researchers after research operations resort to extracting general universal judgments, formulating universal rules and scientific laws, then they place these judgments, rules, and laws as foundations upon which to build and benefit from them in all fields of theoretical and practical knowledge.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage describes the fundamental methodological operations of division (taqsim) and collection (jam') in the process of acquiring knowledge. The author begins by reminding the reader that the universal can be divided into particulars, which in turn may be further classified into species, varieties, or individuals. Examples are given from human classification: división by color (white, black, red, yellow), by geography (African, Asian, European), by intelligence, health, religion, and morality. Then the division of species into individuals is exemplified by personal names (Sa'd, Basim, etc.). The author then explains the converse operation: particulars that share a common meaning can be collected mentally under a single universal. This is illustrated with examples like 'unicorn' for any animal with one horn, 'quadruped' for four-legged animals, 'mammal' for suckling animals, 'white' for anything white, and 'tall' for anything tall. The passage then links these operations to the broader concept of whole and parts, noting that every composite can be analyzed into its simpler components. The text explicitly defines the two operations: dividing the universal into its particulars and varieties, and collecting scattered particulars into their universals. The benefits are detailed: division allows thorough study of each part, while collection after partial study yields universal rules that summarize knowledge without losing applicability. This collection also generates new knowledge by deriving universal judgments. The mind naturally seeks such universals to avoid memorizing every particular and to facilitate application to new instances. The passage concludes by stating that researchers, after research, extract general judgments and formulate universal rules and scientific laws as foundations for all knowledge fields.

Collection of Particulars into Universals
Author describes the process of collecting particulars into universals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how particulars sharing a common attribute are collected under a universal concept, as illustrated in the passage.

Core Idea
Collection unites scattered particulars into universal rules, saving memory and enabling application.

This lesson focuses on the complementary operation of collection (jam‘). After dividing universals and studying their parts in detail, the mind collects similar particulars under a universal concept. The author gives examples like 'quadruped' and 'mammal' to show how any shared attribute can form a universal. This operation is essential for formulating general principles in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particulars that share a common attribute
Look for a set of things that have a shared description. In the passage, animals that walk on four legs share the attribute 'quadruped'.
The shared attribute can be any description, not necessarily essential.
2
Formulate a universal name based on that attribute
Derive a collective name from the shared attribute. Examples: 'unicorn' from 'one horn', 'mammal' from 'suckling young'.
The universal name applies to every particular that possesses the attribute.
3
Understand the purpose of collection
Collection allows us to group similar judgments and formulate universal rules, which summarize knowledge and make it easier to apply to new instances.
The passage emphasizes that collection yields 'universals of judgments'.
4
Apply to Islamic sciences
Consider how in Hadith studies, a collector gathers all hadiths on a specific topic (e.g., rulings on prayer) and derives a general ruling that applies to all particular cases.
This operation is used in Fiqh to formulate qawa'id fiqhiyya (legal maxims).

الكلي ينقسم كما عرفنا إلى جزئيات وهذه الجزئيات تكون أنواعا كانقسام الجنس إلى أنواعه وتكون أصنافا أو أفرادا كانقسام النوع إلى أصنافه أو أفراده ومثال انقسام النوع إلى أصنافه انقسام الإنسان إلى أبيض وأسود وأحمر وأصفر وانقسامه إلى إفريقي وآسيوي وأوروبي وانقسامه إلى ذكي وبليد وما بينهما وانقسامه إلى صحيح وعليل وانقسامه إلى مؤمن وكافر وإلى تقي وفاجر وهكذا لا تكاد تنحصر تقسيمات الأصناف باختلاف الاعتبارات ومثال انقسام النوع إلى أفراده انقسام الإنسان إلى سعد وباسم وجميل وسعدية وباسمة وجميلة وهكذا إلى سائر أفراد نوع الإنسان والجزئيات المشتركة في معنى يطلق هذا المعنى على كل منها يمكن أن تجمع ذهنا في كلي واحد فحيث نجد أشياء مشتركة في معنى جامع لها ولو بوصف من الأوصاف يمكن أن نجمعها تحت اسم كلي جامع مشتق من هذا الوصف المشترك فوحيد القرن كلي يمكن أن يطلق على كل حيوان ذي قرن واحد فقط وذوات القوائم الأربع كلي نجمع تحته كل حيوان يمشي على أربع قوائم والثديي كلي نجمع تحته كل حيوان يرضع بثدي له أو هو من نوع ما يرضع بثدي له والأبيض كلي نجمع تحته كل ذي لون أبيض من أي نوع ومن أي جنس والطويل كذلك وهكذا إلى ما لا حصر له والكل يتألف كما عرفنا سابقا من أجزاء والأجزاء البسيطة أو المركبة قابلة للتركيب بوجه ما سواء أكان هذا التركيب على وجه له نظير في التركيبات الطبيعية أو على وجه آخر يفترضه الخيال وكل مركب قابل للتحليل إلى أجزائه الصغيرة وعناصره الأولى. أ - عمليات التقسيم والجمع فمن الوسائل النافعة جدا أو الضرورية في كثير من الأحيان في مجال اكتساب المعارف الحسية أو الاستنباطية النظرية أو العملية عمليات التقسيم والجمع أي تقسيم الكلي إلى جزئياته وإلى أصنافه وجمع الجزئيات المتفرقة في كلياتها ففي التقسيم لكليات الأشياء تيسير لدراسة كل قسم دراسة مستوعبة أو أكثر إحاطة بالصفات والخصائص وبعد الدراسة الجزئية التفصيلية واستنباط الأحكام منها تعود العملية إلى جمع الأحكام الجزئية المتماثلة أو جمع الأشباه والنظائر وإعطائها صفة القاعدة الكلية الشاملة لأفراد الصنف أو لأفراد النوع أو لأفراد الجنس القريب أو البعيد ففي هذا الجمع اختصار للمعرفة وإيجاز فيها دون الإخلال بالمقصود منها ودون الإخلال بتطبيقاتها بل هي أيسر وأحكم لضبط الجزئيات دون إخلال وفي هذا الجمع أيضا معرفة جديدة تكتسب فيها كليات الأحكام ومن طبيعة الفكر ميله دائما إلى إدراك كليات الأحكام وكليات القضايا ليوفر على نفسه حفظ كل جزئي وصفاته وخصائصه وليستوعب في أقصر مدة أوسع ما يمكن من معرفة وليتيسر له تطبيق ما استوعب من أحكام كلية على كل جزئي يتعرض له من الجزئيات الداخلة في عموم ما ينطبق عليه الحكم الكلي ولو لم يكن له بخصوصه سابق معرفة به لذلك يلجأ الباحثون بعد عمليات البحث إلى استخلاص الأحكام الكلية العامة وصوغ القواعد الكلية والقوانين العلمية ثم يضعون هذه الأحكام والقواعد والقوانين أسسا يبنى عليها وينتفع بها في كل مجالات المعرفة النظرية والتطبيقية
Research Tools: Operations of Division and Collection, Analysis and Composition. The universal is divided - as we have known - into particulars, and these particulars become types, like the division of genus into its species, and they become varieties or individuals, like the division of species into its varieties or its individuals. An example of the division of species into its varieties: the division of human into white, black, red, yellow; and its division into African, Asian, European; and its division into intelligent, stupid and what is between them; and its division into healthy and sick; and its division into believer and disbeliever, and into pious and immoral; and so on, the divisions of varieties are almost unlimited by different considerations. An example of the division of species into its individuals: the division of human into Sa'd, Basim, and Jamil, and Sa'diyah, Basimah, and Jamilah, and so on to the rest of the individuals of the human species. Particulars that share a meaning that this meaning is applied to each of them can be collected mentally into one universal. So wherever we find things sharing a comprehensive meaning, even by one description, we can collect them under a collective universal name derived from this shared description. Thus unicorn is a universal that can be applied to every animal with only one horn. And quadruped is a universal under which we collect every animal that walks on four legs. And mammal is a universal under which we collect every animal that suckles with its breast, or is of the kind that suckles with its breast. And white is a universal under which we collect everything having white color from any species and any genus. And tall likewise. And so on ad infinitum. The whole - as we have known previously - consists of parts. The simple or composite parts are liable to composition in some way, whether this composition is of a kind that has a counterpart in natural compositions, or of another kind that the imagination posits. And every composite is subject to analysis into its small parts and its primary elements. A - Operations of Division and Collection: Among the very useful or often necessary means in the field of acquiring sensory or inferential knowledge, theoretical or practical, are the operations of division and collection, i.e., dividing the universal into its particulars and its varieties, and collecting scattered particulars into their universals. For in the division of universals of things, there is facilitation for studying each section comprehensively, or more encompassing of attributes and characteristics. And after the detailed partial study and the deduction of judgments from them, the operation returns to collecting similar partial judgments, or collecting similars and analogues, and giving them the character of the universal rule that encompasses the individuals of the variety, or the individuals of the species, or the individuals of the proximate or remote genus. For in this collection there is a summarization of knowledge and conciseness in it without violating its intended purpose, and without violating its applications; rather it is easier and more precise for controlling the particulars without violation. And in this collection there is also new knowledge, in which universals of judgments are acquired. And it is in the nature of the mind to always tend to perceive universals of judgments and universals of propositions, to spare itself the memorization of every particular and its attributes and characteristics, and to encompass in the shortest time the widest possible knowledge, and to facilitate for itself the application of what it has encompassed of universal judgments to every particular it encounters among the particulars that fall under the generality to which the universal judgment applies, even if it had no prior knowledge of it specifically. Therefore, researchers after research operations resort to extracting general universal judgments, formulating universal rules and scientific laws, then they place these judgments, rules, and laws as foundations upon which to build and benefit from them in all fields of theoretical and practical knowledge.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage describes the fundamental methodological operations of division (taqsim) and collection (jam') in the process of acquiring knowledge. The author begins by reminding the reader that the universal can be divided into particulars, which in turn may be further classified into species, varieties, or individuals. Examples are given from human classification: división by color (white, black, red, yellow), by geography (African, Asian, European), by intelligence, health, religion, and morality. Then the division of species into individuals is exemplified by personal names (Sa'd, Basim, etc.). The author then explains the converse operation: particulars that share a common meaning can be collected mentally under a single universal. This is illustrated with examples like 'unicorn' for any animal with one horn, 'quadruped' for four-legged animals, 'mammal' for suckling animals, 'white' for anything white, and 'tall' for anything tall. The passage then links these operations to the broader concept of whole and parts, noting that every composite can be analyzed into its simpler components. The text explicitly defines the two operations: dividing the universal into its particulars and varieties, and collecting scattered particulars into their universals. The benefits are detailed: division allows thorough study of each part, while collection after partial study yields universal rules that summarize knowledge without losing applicability. This collection also generates new knowledge by deriving universal judgments. The mind naturally seeks such universals to avoid memorizing every particular and to facilitate application to new instances. The passage concludes by stating that researchers, after research, extract general judgments and formulate universal rules and scientific laws as foundations for all knowledge fields.

Analysis and Synthesis: Definitions and Necessity
Defines analysis and synthesis and their necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define analysis and synthesis and explain their complementary roles in acquiring knowledge.

Core Idea
Analysis breaks down wholes into parts; synthesis rebuilds parts to serve human goals.

In this passage, the author introduces analysis and synthesis as essential tools for both sensory and inferential knowledge. Understanding these operations is foundational to the Islamic intellectual tradition, where scholars from jurisprudence to theology rely on decomposing concepts and recomposing arguments. Let's explore how the author defines these operations and why they are necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of analysis
Read the opening sentences where the author defines 'analysis'. Note that it involves dividing a whole into its constituent parts, studying each part's attributes, and understanding their interrelations.
The whole can be simple or compound; analysis reveals the structure of the whole.
2
Identify the definition of synthesis
The author describes synthesis after analysis: either recombining the parts or inventing a new composition. Note the role of imagination and human goals in synthesis.
Synthesis is not arbitrary; it must serve a purpose.
3
Understand the necessity of analysis
Look for the statement: 'Without analysis, it is impossible to study the whole as a single unit.' The author argues that complex wholes must be decomposed to be understood.
This principle applies across sciences.
4
Relate to the medical example
The author illustrates with medical research: the human body and soul are analyzed, then general judgments are applied. This shows the practical cycle of analysis and synthesis.
The example grounds the abstract concepts in a real scientific practice.

فيه، وتأثرها منه، وخدمات كلّ منها للآخر، وتعاونة معه . وبعد عمليات التحليل يصدر أحكامه العامة التي توصل إليها، ثم يجري تطبيقاته العملية وفق ما توصل إليه هو أو غيره من الباحثين من أحكام عامة، ووفق ما أكثر وضوحاً منه في غيرها. قال الإمام الغزالي في معيار العلم عند بحث مقدمات القياس:
B - Operations of analysis and synthesis: Among the very useful, or often necessary, means in the field of acquiring sensory knowledge or theoretical or practical inferential knowledge are the operations of analysis and synthesis. By analysis is meant the division of the whole into its constituent parts, whether simple or compound, and the study of each part individually to know its attributes, characteristics, and functions, then considering the way the parts are interconnected, and each part performing its own function according to its position in the whole, until the whole is assembled from them and performs its greater function based on the cooperation of the parts. After the operations of analysis of a single thing, or a number of things, and after considering the attributes and characteristics of the parts and what functions they can perform, comes the operation of recombination, or the invention of a new composition imagined by the imagination, noting the compatibility between the imagined composition and one of the human goals in life. The researcher in human medicine must analyze the human being into its constituent parts, whether physical or psychological, then study each organ and each part of his soul in detailed anatomical study; and study flesh, blood, bone, the nervous system, cells and their functions, effects, and ailments, and know the elements that compose them, what affects them, what results from them, and what functions they perform within the overall system. In his study of the human soul, he studies its basic elements, what affects it, its relationship with the body, its influence on it, its being influenced by it, the services of each to the other, and its cooperation with it. After the operations of analysis, he issues the general judgments he has reached, then carries out his practical applications according to what he or other researchers have reached of general judgments, and according to what he observes of special cases in the reality of the patient he treats. The chemical researcher analyzes materials into their simple elements or compound parts as much as possible for him, and after studying these elements and their properties, he is able to invent new compounds he imagines, and conduct experiments on them, and observe the results of the experiment, then record the properties of the new compound, and what benefits this new compound can provide that serve humanity and what interests it can achieve for peace and prosperity, or for power and war, or otherwise. Without analysis, it is impossible for the researcher to study the whole as a single unit, while it is composed of parts, and parts are composed of finer parts, and so on descending to finer and finer, until the first simple elements. Divisions of analysis and synthesis: Each of analysis and synthesis is divided into two parts: The first part: mental (logical). The second part: material (experimental). A - Mental analysis: It is an intellectual operation based on a mental isolation of the attributes of the thing being analyzed, or isolation of its properties, or isolation of its parts from each other, with the aim of knowing its reality. It is therefore an abstract intellectual operation carried out by the researcher to arrive at the parts of a meaning composed of several meanings. For the meaning of 'human' is a whole composed of parts, and by research it becomes clear to us that its essential components from its parts are two parts: animality and rationality, and this result is reached through mental (logical) analysis. This logical analysis occurs in various sciences, but it is more evident in mathematical sciences than in others. Imam al-Ghazali said in Mi'yar al-'Ilm, when discussing the premises of the syllogism:
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological and methodological exposition on the operations of analysis and synthesis as essential tools for acquiring knowledge, both empirical and inferential. The author first defines analysis as the division of a whole into its constituent parts—simple or compound—and studying each part's attributes, characteristics, and functions, as well as their interrelations within the whole. Synthesis follows analysis, either by recombining the parts or creating new compositions guided by human goals. The author illustrates with examples from medicine and chemistry: the medical researcher analyzes the human body and soul to then apply general judgments to specific cases; the chemical researcher analyzes substances into elements and then synthesizes new compounds with beneficial properties. Without analysis, the researcher cannot study a complex whole. The passage then divides analysis and synthesis into two types: mental (logical) and material (experimental). Mental analysis is an abstract intellectual process of isolating attributes or parts to grasp the reality of a composite concept, such as analyzing the meaning of 'human' into animality and rationality. The author notes that logical analysis appears in all sciences but is clearest in mathematics. The passage concludes by referencing Imam al-Ghazali's 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm', indicating that the following discussion will engage with Ghazali's treatment of the premises of the syllogism.

تركيب

Mental vs. Material Analysis
Classifies analysis into mental and material

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mental (logical) analysis and material (experimental) analysis using examples from the passage.

Core Idea
Mental analysis isolates concepts; material analysis dissects physical substances.

The passage classifies analysis into two kinds: mental (logical) and material (experimental). This distinction is vital for understanding how different fields approach knowledge. In Islamic sciences, mental analysis is used in theology and jurisprudence, while material analysis is relevant to empirical observations of the natural world. Let's examine how the author defines each type.

Guided Path
1
Locate the classification
Find the section where the author divides analysis into two parts. Notice the terms 'aqli (logical) and madi (experimental).
This division is explicit: 'القسم الأول: عقلي (منطقي). القسم الثاني: مادي (تجريبي).'
2
Understand mental analysis
Read the definition of mental analysis: an intellectual operation isolating attributes or parts to know the reality of a thing. The example given is the analysis of 'human' into animality and rationality.
Mental analysis is abstract; it deals with meanings and concepts.
3
Understand material analysis
The passage earlier described material analysis through the examples of medical and chemical research. This involves physically dividing substances and studying their properties experimentally.
Material analysis is empirical and sensory.
4
Contrast the two
Compare the 'human' example (mental) with the chemical analysis example (material). Note the difference in method and object: concepts versus physical substances.
The author emphasizes that logical analysis is clearer in mathematics, where concepts are most abstract.

الكل إلى أجزائه التي يتألف منها، بسيطة كانت أو مركبة، ودراسة كل جزء منها دراسة خاصة به، لمعرفة صفاته، وخصائصه، ووظائفه، ثم النظر في وجه ترابط الأجزاء بعضها ببعض، وأداء كل جزء منها وظيفته الخاصة به، بحسب موضعه من الكل، حتى اجتمع منها الكل فأدى وظيفته الكبرى القائمة على تعاون الأجزاء . وبعد عمليات التحليل للشيء الواحد، أو لعدد من الأشياء، وبعد النظر في صفات الأجزاء وخصائصها، وما يمكن أن تقوم به من وظائف، تأتي عملية إعادة التركيب، أو ابتكار تركيب جديد يفترضه التخيل، ملاحظاً الملاءمة بين التركيب الذي يتخيله وبين غاية من غايات الإنسان في الحياة . إن الباحث في طب الإنسان لا بد له من أن يُحلّل الإنسان إلى أجزائه التي يتألف منها، جسدية كانت أو نفسية، ثم يدرس كل عضو من أعضائه وكلّ جزء من أجزاء نفسه دراسة تشريحية تفصيلية؛ ويدرس اللحم والدم والعظم والجملة العصبية والخلايا ووظائفها وآثارها وعللها، ويعرف العناصر التي تتركب منها، وما يؤثر عليها، وما ينتج عنها، وما تقوم به من وظائف ضمن الجهاز الكلي . وفي دراسته لنفس الإنسان يدرس عناصرها الأساسية، وما يؤثر فيها، وعلاقاتها بالجسد وتأثيرها فيه، وتأثرها منه، وخدمات كلّ منها للآخر، وتعاونة معه . وبعد عمليات التحليل يصدر أحكامه العامة التي توصل إليها، ثم يجري تطبيقاته العملية وفق ما توصل إليه هو أو غيره من الباحثين من أحكام عامة، ووفق ما يلاحظ من حالات خاصة في واقع الشخص الذي يعالجه . والباحث الكيميائي يُحلّل المواد إلى عناصرها البسيطة أو أجزائها المركبة وفق ما يتيسر له، وبعد دراسة هذه العناصر ودراسة خصائصها باستطاعته أن يبتكر مركبات جديدة يفترضها، ويجري التجربة عليها، ويلاحظ نتائج التجربة، فيسجل خصائص المركب الجديد، وما يمكن أن يقدّمه هذا المركب الجديد من فوائد تخدم الإنسان وما يمكن أن يحقق من مصالح للسلم والرفاهية، أو للقوة والحرب، أو غير ذلك. وبغير التحليل يتعذر على الباحث دراسة الكل جملة واحدة، وهو مؤلف من أجزاء، والأجزاء مؤلفة من أجزاء أدق منها، وهكذا تنازلاً إلى الأدق فالأدق، حتى العناصر البسيطة الأولى. أقسام التحليل والتركيب: وكلٌّ من التحليل والتركيب ينقسم إلى قسمين: القسم الأول: عقلي (منطقي). القسم الثاني: مادي (تجريبي). أ ـ فالتحليل العقلي: هو عملية فكرية تقوم على عزل ذهني لصفات الشيء الموضوع للتحليل، أو عزل لخواصه، أو عزل لأجزائه بعضها عن بعض، بقصد معرفة حقيقته. فهو إذن عملية فكرية تجريدية يقوم بها الباحث للوصول إلى أجزاء المعنى المركب من عدة معانٍ. فمعنى الإنسان هو كلٌّ مركب من أجزاء، وبالبحث يتبين لنا أن المقوّم الأساسي له من أجزائه جزءان، هما الحيوانية والناطقية، وهذه النتيجة إنما توصلنا إليها عن طريق التحليل العقلي (المنطقي). وهذا التحليل المنطقي يكون في مختلف العلوم، بيد أنه في العلوم الرياضية أكثر وضوحاً منه في غيرها. قال الإمام الغزالي في معيار العلم عند بحث مقدمات القياس:
B - Operations of analysis and synthesis: Among the very useful, or often necessary, means in the field of acquiring sensory knowledge or theoretical or practical inferential knowledge are the operations of analysis and synthesis. By analysis is meant the division of the whole into its constituent parts, whether simple or compound, and the study of each part individually to know its attributes, characteristics, and functions, then considering the way the parts are interconnected, and each part performing its own function according to its position in the whole, until the whole is assembled from them and performs its greater function based on the cooperation of the parts. After the operations of analysis of a single thing, or a number of things, and after considering the attributes and characteristics of the parts and what functions they can perform, comes the operation of recombination, or the invention of a new composition imagined by the imagination, noting the compatibility between the imagined composition and one of the human goals in life. The researcher in human medicine must analyze the human being into its constituent parts, whether physical or psychological, then study each organ and each part of his soul in detailed anatomical study; and study flesh, blood, bone, the nervous system, cells and their functions, effects, and ailments, and know the elements that compose them, what affects them, what results from them, and what functions they perform within the overall system. In his study of the human soul, he studies its basic elements, what affects it, its relationship with the body, its influence on it, its being influenced by it, the services of each to the other, and its cooperation with it. After the operations of analysis, he issues the general judgments he has reached, then carries out his practical applications according to what he or other researchers have reached of general judgments, and according to what he observes of special cases in the reality of the patient he treats. The chemical researcher analyzes materials into their simple elements or compound parts as much as possible for him, and after studying these elements and their properties, he is able to invent new compounds he imagines, and conduct experiments on them, and observe the results of the experiment, then record the properties of the new compound, and what benefits this new compound can provide that serve humanity and what interests it can achieve for peace and prosperity, or for power and war, or otherwise. Without analysis, it is impossible for the researcher to study the whole as a single unit, while it is composed of parts, and parts are composed of finer parts, and so on descending to finer and finer, until the first simple elements. Divisions of analysis and synthesis: Each of analysis and synthesis is divided into two parts: The first part: mental (logical). The second part: material (experimental). A - Mental analysis: It is an intellectual operation based on a mental isolation of the attributes of the thing being analyzed, or isolation of its properties, or isolation of its parts from each other, with the aim of knowing its reality. It is therefore an abstract intellectual operation carried out by the researcher to arrive at the parts of a meaning composed of several meanings. For the meaning of 'human' is a whole composed of parts, and by research it becomes clear to us that its essential components from its parts are two parts: animality and rationality, and this result is reached through mental (logical) analysis. This logical analysis occurs in various sciences, but it is more evident in mathematical sciences than in others. Imam al-Ghazali said in Mi'yar al-'Ilm, when discussing the premises of the syllogism:
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological and methodological exposition on the operations of analysis and synthesis as essential tools for acquiring knowledge, both empirical and inferential. The author first defines analysis as the division of a whole into its constituent parts—simple or compound—and studying each part's attributes, characteristics, and functions, as well as their interrelations within the whole. Synthesis follows analysis, either by recombining the parts or creating new compositions guided by human goals. The author illustrates with examples from medicine and chemistry: the medical researcher analyzes the human body and soul to then apply general judgments to specific cases; the chemical researcher analyzes substances into elements and then synthesizes new compounds with beneficial properties. Without analysis, the researcher cannot study a complex whole. The passage then divides analysis and synthesis into two types: mental (logical) and material (experimental). Mental analysis is an abstract intellectual process of isolating attributes or parts to grasp the reality of a composite concept, such as analyzing the meaning of 'human' into animality and rationality. The author notes that logical analysis appears in all sciences but is clearest in mathematics. The passage concludes by referencing Imam al-Ghazali's 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm', indicating that the following discussion will engage with Ghazali's treatment of the premises of the syllogism.

Key Terms
تحليل عقلي
تحليل مادي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main characteristic of mental (logical) analysis?
A) It involves physical dissection of materials
B) It is an abstract intellectual operation isolating attributes or parts of a meaning
C) It is only used in mathematics
D) It relies on experimental observation

Key Takeaway
Mental analysis is a conceptual operation that isolates the essential components of a meaning, while material analysis involves physical or experimental decomposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each of the following as mental or material analysis: (a) A chemist analyzing water into hydrogen and oxygen; (b) A mutakallim analyzing 'ilm (knowledge) into necessary and acquired types; (c) A physician dissecting a cadaver to study organs; (d) A grammarian analyzing a sentence into subject and predicate.
?
Using the passage's example of analyzing 'human' into animality and rationality, perform a similar mental analysis on the concept of 'wudu' (ablution) by identifying its essential components according to the Shafi'i school.

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
Necessity of Analysis in Knowledge Acquisition
Argues for the necessity of analysis using examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why analysis is indispensable for studying complex wholes, using examples from medicine and chemistry.

Core Idea
Without analysis, complex wholes cannot be understood or manipulated.

The passage strongly argues that analysis is not optional but necessary for studying any complex whole. Through the vivid examples of medical and chemical research, the author demonstrates that decomposition into parts is the only way to grasp the structure and function of a system. This lesson focuses on that rationale and its implications for Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Find the necessity statement
Locate the sentence: 'Without analysis, it is impossible to study the whole as a single unit.' This is the key claim. Note the reasoning: because the whole is composed of parts, which are themselves composed of finer parts.
This is a foundational epistemological principle.
2
Examine the medical example
Read the detailed description of medical research. The researcher must analyze the human body and soul into organs, cells, etc., then study each part's functions and interrelations.
The example shows that analysis precedes diagnosis and treatment.
3
Examine the chemical example
The chemical researcher analyzes materials into elements, then synthesizes new compounds. Note that analysis enables invention and application.
Both examples highlight that analysis is the first step toward practical benefits.
4
Generalize the principle
Reflect on why the same logic applies to any complex object of study. In Islamic sciences, analyzing a legal ruling or a theological concept follows the same pattern.
The principle is universal: to understand any composite, one must decompose it.

ب - عمليات التحليل والتركيب : ومن الوسائل النافعة جداً، أو الضرورية في كثير من الأحيان، في مجال اكتساب المعارف الحسية أو الاستنباطية النظرية أو العملية، عمليات التحليل والتركيب . ويقصد بالتحليل تجزئة Why does the author consider analysis necessary for studying a whole?
A) Because the whole is more important than its parts

The Division of Analysis and Synthesis into Rational and Material
Author classifies analysis and synthesis into rational and material types using chemistry and logic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify analysis and synthesis into rational and material types and define each type using examples from Islamic logic and science.

Core Idea
Analysis and synthesis split into rational (mental) and material (physical) operations, each serving distinct roles in knowledge.

This passage from Dawabit al-Ma'rifa introduces a crucial methodological distinction: the same acts of breaking down and building up can occur in the mind or in the physical world. Understanding this division helps you see how Islamic sciences integrate intellectual reasoning with empirical investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main processes
Note that the passage treats 'analysis' (tahlil) and 'synthesis' (tarkib) as complementary processes. Analysis breaks down composites, synthesis builds them up.
2
Observe the binary division of each
Each process is divided into two types: rational ('aqli) and material (madi). This is the main classification being taught.
Rational is also called logical; material is also called experimental.
3
Examine rational analysis in detail
Rational analysis is defined as an intellectual process that isolates qualities or parts of a thing to know its reality. The example given is analyzing 'human' into animality and rationality. The author quotes al-Ghazali to reinforce the concept.
This analysis is common in all sciences but most evident in mathematics.
4
Contrast with material analysis and note the role of synthesis
Material analysis is physical separation of composites. The passage highlights its benefits in discovery and innovation. Rational synthesis is the mental construction of a whole from parts, forming an intellectual structure.
Intellectual analysis often precedes material analysis.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حقيقته. فهو إذن عملية فكرية تجريدية يقوم بها الباحث للوصول إلى أجزاء المعنى المركب من عدة معانٍ. فمعنى الإنسان هو كلٌّ مركب من أجزاء، وبالبحث يتبين لنا أن المقوّم الأساسي له من أجزائه جزءان، هما الحيوانية والناطقية، وهذه النتيجة إنما توصلنا إليها عن طريق التحليل العقلي (المنطقي). وهذا التحليل المنطقي يكون في مختلف العلوم، بيد أنه في العلوم الرياضية أكثر وضوحاً منه في غيرها. قال الإمام الغزالي في معيار العلم عند بحث مقدمات القياس: «وكلّ ناظر في شيء مركب فطريقه أن يُحَلّل المركب إلى المفردات، ويبتدىء في النظر في الآحاد، ثم في المركب... فإن كلّ مركب من (مادة) و (صورة) يجب النظر في (مادته) و (صورته)، وما هذا إلّا كمن يريد بناء بيت فحقه أن يهتم بإفراز المواد التي منها يتركب، كاللَّبِن والطين والخشب، ثم يشتغل بالتصوير، وكيفية التنضيد والتركيب». ب ـ والتحليل المادي التجريبي: هو عملية مادية، تقوم على عزل أجزاء المركب المادي عن ارتباطها التركيبي، لاكتشاف حقيقة هذه الأجزاء وصفاتها، وخصائصها، وآثارها، ووجه ارتباطها بالشيء الذي عزلت عنه، وإمكان ارتباطها بأي جزء آخر، إلى غير ذلك مما يمكن بحثه واكتشاف شيء فيه. وبديهي أن هذا التحليل المادي قد أفاد المعارف المادية والعقلية فوائد جَمّة، فقد توسعت به العمليات التجريبية توسعاً عظيماً جداً، وانتهى البحث العلمي به إلى اكتشاف كثير من العناصر التي كانت مجهولة من قبل، ثم استعملت هذه العناصر في مركبات جديدة مفيدة في مجالات كثيرة، كما استخدمت بعض هذه العناصر دون تركيب في مجالات كثيرة أيضاً أفادت الإنسان فوائد جَمّة. وقد لا يمارس الباحث أعمال التحليل المادي قبل أن يقوم بأعمال التحليل الفكري، إذ يكون العمل الفكري في التحليل سابقاً للعمل المادي التجريبي. جـ ـ والتركيب العقلي: هو انتقال الفكر من الأجزاء الصغيرة، أو من العناصر البسيطة، إلى الكل الذي يتركب منها، أو يمكن أن يتركب منها. فيجمع الفكر مثلاً أجزاء متفرقة، ويرتب بينها، ويعقد روابطها، ويؤلف منها كلاً ذا هيكل فكري مترابط، مادّته الأجزاء، وصورته الهيئة الفكرية.
The chemical researcher analyzes materials into their simple elements or composite parts according to what is available to him, and after studying these elements and their properties, he is able to invent new compounds that he hypothesizes, and conducts experiments on them, and observes the results of the experiment, recording the properties of the new compound, and what benefits this new compound can provide to serve humanity and what interests it can achieve for peace and welfare, or for strength and war, or otherwise. Without analysis, it is difficult for the researcher to study the whole as one unit, while it is composed of parts, and the parts are composed of finer parts, and so on descending to the finest, until the first simple elements. Sections of analysis and synthesis: Each of analysis and synthesis is divided into two parts: The first part: rational (logical). The second part: material (experimental). A. Rational analysis: It is an intellectual process based on a mental isolation of the qualities of the thing under analysis, or isolation of its properties, or isolation of its parts from each other, with the aim of knowing its reality. So it is an abstract intellectual process that the researcher performs to reach the parts of a meaning composed of multiple meanings. For example, the meaning of 'human' is a whole composed of parts, and through investigation it becomes clear to us that its fundamental constituents are two parts: animality and rationality. This result is reached through rational (logical) analysis. This logical analysis occurs in various sciences, but it is more evident in mathematical sciences than in others. Imam al-Ghazali said in Mi'yar al-'Ilm, when discussing the premises of syllogism: 'Every observer of something composite should analyze the composite into its simple components, and begin by examining the individuals, then the composite... For every composite of (matter) and (form) must be examined in its (matter) and (form). This is like someone who wants to build a house; his duty is to focus on separating the materials from which it is composed, such as bricks, clay, and wood, then engage in forming and the manner of arranging and combining.' B. Material experimental analysis: It is a material process, based on isolating the parts of the material composite from their structural connection, to discover the reality of these parts and their qualities, properties, effects, the manner of their connection to the thing from which they were isolated, and the possibility of their connection to any other part, and so on to what can be investigated and discovered. Obviously, this material analysis has provided great benefits to material and intellectual knowledge; experimental operations have expanded greatly through it, and scientific research has ended up discovering many elements that were previously unknown, then these elements were used in new beneficial compounds in many fields, as some of these elements were used without composition in many fields that also benefited humanity greatly. The researcher may not undertake material analysis before performing intellectual analysis, for intellectual analysis precedes experimental material work. C. Rational synthesis: It is the transfer of thought from small parts, or from simple elements, to the whole that is composed of them, or that can be composed of them. For example, thought collects scattered parts, arranges them, establishes connections, and composes from them a whole with an interconnected intellectual structure, its matter being the parts, and its form being the intellectual shape.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage provides a classification and definition of analysis and synthesis, dividing each into rational (logical) and material (experimental) types. The author begins with a concrete example from chemistry to illustrate the necessity of analysis in studying composites. Then, the division is stated: each of analysis and synthesis has two parts: rational (logical) and material (experimental). The text then defines rational analysis as an intellectual process of isolating qualities or parts to understand reality. An example is given: the concept of 'human' is analyzed into animality and rationality, which is a result of rational analysis. The author notes that rational analysis is more evident in mathematical sciences. A quote from Imam al-Ghazali supports this, comparing analysis to separating building materials before construction. Next, material analysis is defined as a physical process of isolating parts of a material composite to discover their properties and connections. The benefits of material analysis are highlighted, including the discovery of new elements and their applications. It is noted that intellectual analysis often precedes material analysis. Finally, rational synthesis is defined as the mental process of moving from simple parts to a whole, forming an interconnected intellectual structure. No explicit logical argument is present; the passage is definitional and classificatory, serving as an expansion on the concepts of analysis and synthesis as used in logic and science.

The Principle of Analysis and Material Analysis
Author explains analysis of compounds and defines material experimental analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between intellectual analysis and material experimental analysis and explain their respective roles in investigating compound realities.

Core Idea
Analysis breaks compounds into simples; material analysis isolates physical parts while intellectual analysis precedes it.

In this passage, the author lays out the foundational distinction between two types of analysis: intellectual and material. Understanding this distinction is crucial for anyone investigating compound realities, whether in physics or in conceptual reasoning. The author uses the analogy of building a house to illustrate the importance of first separating raw materials before focusing on form and structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound under investigation
Recognize that any compound object or concept consists of simpler parts. The author mentions 'every compound of matter and form'.
2
Distinguish matter and form
Matter is the material component (like bricks and clay), form is the structural arrangement (like the design of a house).
3
Recognize intellectual analysis
This is the conceptual decomposition of a compound into its mental components, often preceding physical work.
Intellectual analysis is implied in the phrase 'the intellectual work in analysis precedes the material experimental work'.
4
Recognize material experimental analysis
This is the physical isolation of parts from their structural connections to discover their reality, attributes, and potentials.
The author provides a detailed definition: 'isolating the parts... to discover the reality of these parts, their attributes...'
5
Understand the order of analysis
Intellectual analysis typically comes first; you conceive of the parts before physically manipulating them.
The final sentence explicitly states this precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكلّ ناظر في شيء مركب فطريقه أن يُحَلّل المركب إلى المفردات، ويبتدىء في النظر في الآحاد، ثم في المركب... فإن كلّ مركب من (مادة) و (صورة) يجب النظر في (مادته) و (صورته)، وما هذا إلّا كمن يريد بناء بيت فحقه أن يهتم بإفراز المواد التي منها يتركب، كاللَّبِن والطين والخشب، ثم يشتغل بالتصوير، وكيفية التنضيد والتركيب. ب ـ والتحليل المادي التجريبي: هو عملية مادية، تقوم على عزل أجزاء المركب المادي عن ارتباطها التركيبي، لاكتشاف حقيقة هذه الأجزاء وصفاتها، وخصائصها، وآثارها، ووجه ارتباطها بالشيء الذي عزلت عنه، وإمكان ارتباطها بأي جزء آخر، إلى غير ذلك مما يمكن بحثه واكتشاف شيء فيه. وبدهي أن هذا التحليل المادي قد أفاد المعارف المادية والعقلية فوائد جَمّة، فقد توسعت به العمليات التجريبية توسعاً عظيماً جداً، وانتهى البحث العلمي به إلى اكتشاف كثير من العناصر التي كانت مجهولة من قبل، ثم استعملت هذه العناصر في مركبات جديدة مفيدة في مجالات كثيرة، كما استخدمت بعض هذه العناصر دون تركيب في مجالات كثيرة أيضاً أفادت الإنسان فوائد جَمّة. وقد لا يمارس الباحث أعمال التحليل المادي قبل أن يقوم بأعمال التحليل الفكري، إذ يكون العمل الفكري في التحليل سابقاً للعمل المادي التجريبي.
And every investigator of a compound thing has as his method to analyze the compound into the simples, and to begin consideration of the individuals, then of the compound... For every compound consists of (matter) and (form); it is necessary to consider its (matter) and (form). This is nothing but like one who wants to build a house; his right is to concern himself with separating the materials from which it is composed, like bricks, clay, and wood, then occupy himself with the form and the manner of arrangement and composition. B – And material experimental analysis: it is a material process, based on isolating the parts of the material compound from their compositional connection, to discover the reality of these parts, their attributes, properties, effects, the aspect of their connection to the thing from which they were isolated, and the possibility of their connection to any other part, and other things that can be researched and discovered therein. And it is obvious that this material analysis has benefited material and intellectual knowledge great benefits; experimental operations have expanded enormously through it, and scientific research through it has ended in the discovery of many elements that were previously unknown, then these elements were used in new compounds useful in many fields, and some of these elements were used without composition in many fields that also benefited humanity greatly. And the researcher may not practice the works of material analysis before performing works of intellectual analysis, since the intellectual work in analysis precedes the material experimental work.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage outlines the foundational methodology for investigating any compound, whether physical or conceptual. The author begins by stating that anyone examining a compound object must first break it down into its simple components and study those individually before considering the compound as a whole. This is illustrated by the analogy of building a house: one must first prepare the raw materials (bricks, clay, wood) and then focus on the design and arrangement. The author then defines 'material experimental analysis' as a physical process of isolating the parts of a material compound from their structural interconnections. The purpose is to discover the true nature, qualities, and potential interactions of these parts. The author notes that this form of analysis has greatly advanced both material and intellectual knowledge, enabling the discovery of new elements and their beneficial applications. Finally, it is observed that intellectual analysis typically precedes material analysis; the mind must first conceptualize the components before physically handling them. This distinction between intellectual and material analysis is crucial for understanding the subsequent discussion of synthesis.

Key Takeaway

The Concept of Intellectual Synthesis
Definition of intellectual synthesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to restate the definition of intellectual synthesis and identify its key components (parts, whole, mental arrangement).

Core Idea
Intellectual synthesis is the mental assembly of parts into a new coherent structure.

The author begins by defining a fundamental intellectual operation: synthesis. This definition sets the stage for understanding how the mind creates new knowledge and organizes it.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the sentence that begins 'والتركيب العقلي: هو انتقال الفكر...'.
The definition states the movement from parts to whole.
2
Identify the components
What are the starting and ending points? Also note the role of the mind: gathering, arranging, connecting.
3
Distinguish matter and form
The author says the matter is the parts, and the form is the intellectual configuration (الهيئة الفكرية).
This mirrors the hylomorphic analysis in philosophy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جـ ـ والتركيب العقلي: هو انتقال الفكر من الأجزاء الصغيرة، أو من العناصر البسيطة، إلى الكل الذي يتركب منها، أو يمكن أن يتركب منها. فيجمع الفكر مثلاً أجزاء متفرقة، ويرتب بينها، ويعقد روابطها، ويؤلف منها كلاً ذا هيكل فكري مترابط، مادّته الأجزاء، وصورته الهيئة الفكرية المجتمعة التي توصل الفكر إلى تركيبها والتنسيق بينها. يأتي الشاعر مثلاً بفكرة زورق، ثم يأتي بفكرة حمولة من عنبر، ثم يؤلف منهما جميعاً كلاً في صورة، ويشبه بها الهلال. فعملية الشاعر قبل أن يصل إلى التشبيه قامت على تركيب فكري، جمع فيه أجزاء متفرقة كانت حاضرة في ذاكرته، ونسق بينها، وأقام منها صورة جديدة. ويأتي المهندس الميكانيكي مثلاً، فيجمع في مخيلته أجزاء متفرقة مما وعت ذاكرته من عناصر الأشياء، ويؤلف بينها تأليفاً مترابطاً منطقياً، بحسب ما يعلم من قوانين الطبيعة وسننها، ثم ينتهي إلى ابتكار هيكل فكري مترابط، مادته الأجزاء التي جمعها، وصورته الهيئة الفكرية الهندسية التي توصل إليها ابتكاراً. وليكن ما توصل إليه في عملية التركيب الفكري مركبة «برية بحرية جوية» تغوص في الماء وتطير في الجو، وهي ذات شكل خاص، وصفات خاصة، وخصائص تختلف عما سبق أن ابتكره الإنسان في مجال المركبات. ثم يأتي التركيب المادي التجريبي المعملي فينفذ العمل التركيبي الذي قام به الفكر، وقد تُصَدِّق التجربة عمل الفكر، أو تُعدّل منه، أو تكذبه وترفضه، كل هذا لا يؤثر في الموضوع، لأن ما قام به الفكر على كل حال إنما هو عمل تركيبي ما، صدقه الواقع التجريبي أو كذبه. وعملية التركيب العقلي هذه هي وسيلة الباحث إلى الاختراع والابتكار، كما هي طريقة العالم في جمع وحدات المعرفة منسقة في كتب وأبواب وفصول وأقسام وأصناف وأنواع ومباحث ومسائل، ونحو ذلك من دوائر تجتمع فيها أجزاء ذات ترابط، فيتألف منها كل ذو هيئة منطقية.
C – And intellectual synthesis: it is the transfer of thought from the small parts, or from the simple elements, to the whole that is composed of them, or that can be composed of them. So the mind, for example, gathers scattered parts, arranges them, establishes connections between them, and composes from them a whole having an interconnected intellectual structure, its matter being the parts, and its form being the combined intellectual configuration that the mind attains by composing and coordinating them. The poet, for example, brings the idea of a boat, then brings the idea of a cargo of ambergris, then composes from both a whole in a form, and uses it to liken the crescent moon. So the poet's process before reaching the simile was based on an intellectual synthesis, in which he gathered scattered parts present in his memory, coordinated them, and established from them a new image. And the mechanical engineer, for example, gathers in his imagination scattered parts from what his memory has stored of the elements of things, and composes them in an interconnected logical composition, according to what he knows of the laws and customs of nature, then ends up with the invention of an interconnected intellectual structure, its matter being the parts he gathered, and its form being the engineering intellectual configuration that he arrived at by invention. And let what he arrived at in the process of intellectual synthesis be a 'land-sea-air vehicle' that dives in water and flies in the air, having a special shape, special qualities, and properties different from what humanity had previously invented in the field of vehicles. Then comes the experimental material laboratory synthesis, which executes the synthetic work that the intellect performed; and experience may confirm the work of the intellect, or modify it, or falsify and reject it. All this does not affect the subject, because what the intellect did in any case is a synthetic work, whether experiential reality confirms it or falsifies it. And this process of intellectual synthesis is the researcher's means to invention and innovation, as it is the scholar's method of collecting units of knowledge arranged in books, chapters, sections, divisions, categories, types, topics, and problems, and similar circles in which interconnected parts come together, forming a whole with a logical structure.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines and elaborates upon 'intellectual synthesis' (al-tarkib al-'aqli). The author describes it as the mind's movement from small parts or simple elements to a whole that either is composed of them or can be composed of them. The mind gathers scattered fragments, arranges them, establishes connections, and produces a new coherent intellectual structure. Two vivid examples are provided: a poet who combines the ideas of a boat and a cargo of ambergris to form a simile for the crescent moon, and a mechanical engineer who mentally assembles known elements to design a novel amphibious or aerial vehicle. The author stresses that this mental construction is separate from its physical realization; material experiment may confirm, modify, or reject it, but the intellectual synthesis itself remains a valid creative act. Finally, the passage connects intellectual synthesis to scholarly organization, likening the structuring of knowledge into books, chapters, and sections to the same synthetic process. This highlights that synthesis is not only for invention but also for systematic understanding.

Key Terms
تركيب عقلي
هيئة فكرية

Key Takeaway
Intellectual synthesis is the mental process of assembling disparate parts into a coherent whole.

Examples and Applications of Intellectual Synthesis
Illustrative examples of intellectual synthesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how intellectual synthesis operates in poetry, engineering, and scholarly organization.

Core Idea
Intellectual synthesis underlies all creative and systematic work, from poetry to engineering to scholarship.

The author provides vivid examples to show how intellectual synthesis works in practice: a poet crafting a simile, an engineer designing a vehicle, and a scholar organizing knowledge. These illustrate the universality of the process.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the poet's synthesis
What are the two elements the poet brings? How does he combine them into a new image?
The poet's simile is an example of creative synthesis.
2
Analyze the engineer's synthesis
What does the engineer gather from his memory? How does he use natural laws to compose a new design?
The engineer's synthesis leads to invention.
3
Distinguish mental from physical
The author says material experiment may confirm, modify, or reject, but the synthesis itself is still a valid mental act.
This emphasizes the autonomy of intellectual synthesis.
4
Extend to scholarly organization
How does the author compare synthesis to the arrangement of knowledge in books?
Synthesis is the basis for systematic knowledge.

جـ ـ والتركيب العقلي: هو انتقال الفكر من الأجزاء الصغيرة، أو من العناصر البسيطة، إلى الكل الذي يتركب منها، أو يمكن أن يتركب منها. فيجمع الفكر مثلاً أجزاء متفرقة، ويرتب بينها، ويعقد روابطها، ويؤلف منها كلاً ذا هيكل فكري مترابط، مادّته الأجزاء، وصورته الهيئة الفكرية المجتمعة التي توصل الفكر إلى تركيبها والتنسيق بينها. يأتي الشاعر مثلاً بفكرة زورق، ثم يأتي بفكرة حمولة من عنبر، ثم يؤلف منهما جميعاً كلاً في صورة، ويشبه بها الهلال. فعملية الشاعر قبل أن يصل إلى التشبيه قامت على تركيب فكري، جمع فيه أجزاء متفرقة كانت حاضرة في ذاكرته، ونسق بينها، وأقام منها صورة جديدة. ويأتي المهندس الميكانيكي مثلاً، فيجمع في مخيلته أجزاء متفرقة مما وعت ذاكرته من عناصر الأشياء، ويؤلف بينها تأليفاً مترابطاً منطقياً، بحسب ما يعلم من قوانين الطبيعة وسننها، ثم ينتهي إلى ابتكار هيكل فكري مترابط، مادته الأجزاء التي جمعها، وصورته الهيئة الفكرية الهندسية التي توصل إليها ابتكاراً. وليكن ما توصل إليه في عملية التركيب الفكري مركبة «برية بحرية جوية» تغوص في الماء وتطير في الجو، وهي ذات شكل خاص، وصفات خاصة، وخصائص تختلف عما سبق أن ابتكره الإنسان في مجال المركبات. ثم يأتي التركيب المادي التجريبي المعملي فينفذ العمل التركيبي الذي قام به الفكر، وقد تُصَدِّق التجربة عمل الفكر، أو تُعدّل منه، أو تكذبه وترفضه، كل هذا لا يؤثر في الموضوع، لأن ما قام به الفكر على كل حال إنما هو عمل تركيبي ما، صدقه الواقع التجريبي أو كذبه. وعملية التركيب العقلي هذه هي وسيلة الباحث إلى الاختراع والابتكار، كما هي طريقة العالم في جمع وحدات المعرفة منسقة في كتب وأبواب وفصول وأقسام وأصناف وأنواع ومباحث ومسائل، ونحو ذلك من دوائر تجتمع فيها أجزاء ذات ترابط، فيتألف منها كل ذو هيئة منطقية.
C – And intellectual synthesis: it is the transfer of thought from the small parts, or from the simple elements, to the whole that is composed of them, or that can be composed of them. So the mind, for example, gathers scattered parts, arranges them, establishes connections between them, and composes from them a whole having an interconnected intellectual structure, its matter being the parts, and its form being the combined intellectual configuration that the mind attains by composing and coordinating them. The poet, for example, brings the idea of a boat, then brings the idea of a cargo of ambergris, then composes from both a whole in a form, and uses it to liken the crescent moon. So the poet's process before reaching the simile was based on an intellectual synthesis, in which he gathered scattered parts present in his memory, coordinated them, and established from them a new image. And the mechanical engineer, for example, gathers in his imagination scattered parts from what his memory has stored of the elements of things, and composes them in an interconnected logical composition, according to what he knows of the laws and customs of nature, then ends up with the invention of an interconnected intellectual structure, its matter being the parts he gathered, and its form being the engineering intellectual configuration that he arrived at by invention. And let what he arrived at in the process of intellectual synthesis be a 'land-sea-air vehicle' that dives in water and flies in the air, having a special shape, special qualities, and properties different from what humanity had previously invented in the field of vehicles. Then comes the experimental material laboratory synthesis, which executes the synthetic work that the intellect performed; and experience may confirm the work of the intellect, or modify it, or falsify and reject it. All this does not affect the subject, because what the intellect did in any case is a synthetic work, whether experiential reality confirms it or falsifies it. And this process of intellectual synthesis is the researcher's means to invention and innovation, as it is the scholar's method of collecting units of knowledge arranged in books, chapters, sections, divisions, categories, types, topics, and problems, and similar circles in which interconnected parts come together, forming a whole with a logical structure.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines and elaborates upon 'intellectual synthesis' (al-tarkib al-'aqli). The author describes it as the mind's movement from small parts or simple elements to a whole that either is composed of them or can be composed of them. The mind gathers scattered fragments, arranges them, establishes connections, and produces a new coherent intellectual structure. Two vivid examples are provided: a poet who combines the ideas of a boat and a cargo of ambergris to form a simile for the crescent moon, and a mechanical engineer who mentally assembles known elements to design a novel amphibious or aerial vehicle. The author stresses that this mental construction is separate from its physical realization; material experiment may confirm, modify, or reject it, but the intellectual synthesis itself remains a valid creative act. Finally, the passage connects intellectual synthesis to scholarly organization, likening the structuring of knowledge into books, chapters, and sections to the same synthetic process. This highlights that synthesis is not only for invention but also for systematic understanding.

تركيب عقلي
هيئة فكرية
تشبيه
اختراع

Intellectual synthesis is the common thread in creativity, innovation, and systematic knowledge organization.

Material Experimental Synthesis Defined
Author defines material experimental synthesis as the physical combination of material elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify material experimental synthesis and distinguish its inputs from those of intellectual synthesis.

Core Idea
Material synthesis physically builds what the mind plans, using raw or pre-analyzed elements.

This lesson unpacks the definition of 'material experimental synthesis', the final step in a four-part methodological cycle. After intellectual analysis and synthesis, material analysis breaks down physical substances, and now material synthesis recomposes them. Understanding this definition is key to grasping how practical knowledge complements theoretical planning in Islamic sciences, from chemistry to medicine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The Arabic term is 'التركيب المادي التجريبي' (al-tarkib al-madi al-tajribi). Note each component: tarkib (composition), madi (material), tajribi (experimental). This tells us the definition concerns physical, experiment-based assembling.
The term appears at the beginning of the passage.
2
Extract the genus (jins) from the definition
The author says 'هو عملية مادية' (it is a material process). This is the broader category: a physical operation, not a mental one. The genus is 'material process'.
Compare with intellectual synthesis, which is a mental process.
3
Identify the differentia (fasl) that specifies it
The differentia is 'تقوم بالتأليف بين العناصر المادية' (performs the composition between material elements). This distinguishes material synthesis from other material processes like analysis or simple mixing without purpose.
The differentia includes the purpose: to compose or combine.
4
Recognize the two sources of elements
The elements come from two sources: 'الجاهزة في الطبيعة' (ready in nature) or 'التي انتهت إليها أعمال التحليل المادي' (those resulting from material analysis). This means synthesis can use raw materials or processed ones.
This links directly to material analysis, the preceding step.
5
Place the definition in the methodological sequence
Material synthesis is the fourth step: intellectual analysis → intellectual synthesis → material analysis → material synthesis. It is the practical culmination that realizes the intellectual plan in the physical world.
Understanding this sequence helps avoid confusing synthesis with analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د ـ والتركيب المادي التجريبي : هو عملية مادية تقوم بالتأليف بين العناصر المادية الجاهزة في الطبيعة أو التي انتهت إليها أعمال التحليل المادي.
D – And material experimental synthesis: it is a material process that performs the composition between material elements ready in nature or those that have resulted from the works of material analysis.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This very brief passage provides a concise definition of 'material experimental synthesis' (al-tarkib al-madi al-tajribi). It is presented as the fourth and final methodological step in the sequence. The author defines it as a physical process that brings together material elements to form a compound. These elements can be either directly available in nature (like raw materials) or obtained through previous material analysis (the process described in section B). Thus, material synthesis is the practical counterpart to intellectual synthesis; it is the actual construction that follows mental planning. This passage completes the methodological cycle from analysis to synthesis, both intellectual and material.

Key Terms
تركيب مادي تجريبي (tarkib madi tajribi): A physical process of composing material elements that are either naturally available or obtained through prior material analysis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, from what sources do the elements for material experimental synthesis come?
A) Only from the intellectual synthesis of the mind.
B) From elements ready in nature or resulting from material analysis.
C) Only from naturally occurring raw materials.
D) From previously completed material syntheses.

Key Takeaway
Material experimental synthesis is the physical composition of elements from nature or prior analysis, completing the analysis-synthesis cycle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each step as intellectual analysis, intellectual synthesis, material analysis, or material experimental synthesis: (a) A jurist compares hadiths on types of water. (b) A chemist heats a substance to separate its components. (c) An engineer mixes cement, sand, and water to create concrete. (d) A mutakallim deduces the attributes of Allah from creation.
?
